He said, and the author of this book, after I have completed for you, my sons, this book which is a part of medicine with its perfection and having reached its utmost clarity and explanation, I saw that I should complete it for you with this chapter which is a part of manual practice.
For the practice of manual skills has been neglected in our country and in our time, almost to the point that its science is forgotten and its traces are lost. What remained of it were mere illustrations in the books of the ancients, which have been smeared by hands and marred by errors to such an extent that their meanings are obscured and their benefits lost.
Therefore, I saw fit to revive it and compile this chapter in the manner of explanation, clarification, and conciseness, and to provide illustrations of the shapes of tools and other instruments of practice, for this adds to the clarity and meets the needs of those who require it.
And the reason why there is no skilled craftsman in our time is that the art of medicine is lengthy, and it is appropriate for one who practices it to first excel in the science of anatomy, as described by Galen. Until he is proficient in the benefits, nature, and mixtures of the limbs, their connections and separations, knowledge of the bones, nerves, muscles, their number, exits, pulsating and calm vessels, and the locations of their exits.
Abqarat said, "Medical practitioners are numerous in name but few in reality, especially in the art of surgery. We have mentioned this at the beginning of this book.
Because those who are not knowledgeable about what we have mentioned regarding dissection will inevitably fall into errors that kill people, as I have often witnessed among those who pretend to be learned in this field without any knowledge or understanding.
I once saw an ignorant physician cut into a worm-like swelling on the neck of a woman, and he severed some of the blood vessels of the neck, causing the woman to bleed until she died in front of him.
I saw another physician who, in removing a large stone from a man's tooth, made a mistake and removed part of the jawbone with it. The man died after about three days, and I was called to remove it. When I saw the size of the stone and the condition of the patient, I did not think he could survive it.
I also saw another physician who was famous among some of the leaders in our country for his medical expertise.
So he told a certain black slave of his, who had a fracture near the ankle along with a wound. The physician, in his ignorance, hurried and secured the fracture over the wound using tight bandages and splints, leaving no space for the wound to breathe.
Then let him loose to his desires, and leave him for days, and command him not to wear the bandage until his shin and foot swell up, and observe the destruction.
I called him, so he hastened to release the bandage and found relief and freedom from his pain, except that the gangrene had taken over the limb, and I was unable to revive it.
The gangrene continued to spread in the limb until it perished.
I saw another physician cauterize and burn a cancerous tumor, and after several days the patient's pain increased because the cancer was composed of black bile, so it should not be exposed to cold iron.
Except if it is in a limb that can be amputated completely.
And for this, my sons, it is incumbent upon you to learn that the work of surgery consists of two parts: safe work and dangerous work in most cases.
I have warned in every place that this book mentions the work which carries risk and fear, so it is incumbent upon you to beware of it and refuse it.
Lest the ignorant find a way to criticize and blame, so take for yourselves diligence and caution, and for your patients, compassion and steadfastness.
The best way leading to safety and the praiseworthy outcome is used, and the dangerous diseases that are difficult to treat are avoided.
And purify yourselves from what you fear may bring uncertainty into your religion and worldly affairs, for it is the best provision for your journey and raises your status in this life and the hereafter according to your worth.
Therefore, Galen said in some of his advices: "Do not treat a bad disease lest you become bad physicians.
This article has been divided into three chapters.
Chapter One
In it, the cautery by fire and the cautery by strong medication are described and arranged from the horn to the foot, with illustrations of the instruments and cautery irons, and everything needed for manual operation.
Chapter Two
In it, incision, cupping, bloodletting, venesection, surgery, and the extraction of arrows, and all such matters are described and arranged with illustrations of the instruments.
Chapter Three
In it, fractures and dislocations, the treatment of sciatica, and similar matters are described and arranged from the head to the foot with illustrations of the instruments.
Chapter One
On Cautery.
Before discussing its use, it is necessary to mention its benefits and harms, and in which temperament it should be used.
I say that the speech on the benefit and harm of cupping is long and precise knowledge, hidden secret, and a group of sages have spoken about it.
And they differed on it, and from their speech there remains only a little, for fear of becoming lengthy.
I say that cupping benefits all types of ailments, whether with or without bloodletting, except for two types: hot temperament without bleeding and dry temperament without bleeding.
As for the dry temperament with bloodletting, they differed on it; some said that cupping is beneficial in this case, while others disagreed, saying that cupping is not suitable for a disease of heat and dryness because the nature of fire is heat and dryness.
It is impossible to cure a hot and dry disease with a hot and dry remedy, but those who say the opposite claim that cupping with fire may benefit from a hot and dry disease occurring in human bodies. Because when you add the human body and its moisture to the temperament of fire, it makes the human body cold.
And I say, following his statement, because experience has revealed this to me many times; however, it is not proper for anyone to consider this matter except one who has practiced and trained thoroughly in the art of cupping. "And he stopped at the difference of humors in people and the nature of diseases within them, their causes, symptoms, and duration.
"As for the rest of the humors, you should not fear them, especially the cold and moist diseases, as all physicians agree on their treatment and do not differ in the benefit of cupping therapy for them.
"And know, O sons, that the secret of treatment by cupping with fire and its superiority over cupping with burnt medicine is that fire is a unique substance that does not exceed the function of the member being treated, nor does it harm another connected member except for slight harm.
"And cupping with burnt medicine may exceed its function to what is beyond the members and sometimes causes a disease in the member that makes its treatment difficult, and sometimes it kills. Fire, due to its nobility and the honor of its substance, does not do this except when used excessively.
"This has been clarified to us through experience over a long period of service and care for the profession, and by paying attention to the facts of the matter.
"And for this reason, I have dispensed with lengthy discourse, though if it were not unsuitable for this book of mine, I would have presented to you a profound secret about fire and its method of operation in bodies, driving out diseases with philosophical arguments that prove the essence of understanding.
Know, O sons, that they have differed on the time suitable for cauterization, and considered the best time to be in spring.
And I say that cauterization can be suitable at any time, for the harm caused by time is less than the benefit obtained from cauterization. Especially if the cauterization is for severe, urgent, and life-threatening conditions that do not tolerate delay, lest it be followed by disfigurement greater than any harm inflicted by time.
And do not be deceived, O sons, by what the common people and ignorant physicians think: that the cauterization which cures a disease can never recur or make it chronic.
The matter is not as they thought, for cauterization is like a medicine that adjusts the temperament and dries the humors which are the cause of the conditions.
But cauterization is preferred over medicine for its quick effectiveness, the strength of its action, and the intensity of its power.
And the disease may recur at some point in time, depending on the temperament of the patient and the strength and nature of the disease, as well as what is prepared in the body from the accumulation of excess humors in it, and his neglect of himself in acquiring nourishment and similar causes.
O God, do not let the disease for which the knife is used be a delicate disease or in a limb with little excess flesh and moisture. Like cutting a tooth to relieve pain and similar things, it may not recur, and that would be in the least amount.
As for the common saying that surgery is the last resort in medicine, it is a correct statement, except for what they believe, which is that there is no cure either by medicine or by other means after the incision, and the matter is contrary to that.
The meaning of "surgery is the last resort in medicine" is that when we have used all means of treatment for a disease and those drugs did not cure, then we use another thing, which is surgery, and it cures. From this comes the saying: "Surgery is the last resort in medicine. Not in the sense that the common people and many of the ignorant physicians understand it.
And it has been mentioned before that cutting with gold is better than cutting with iron, and they said this because of the balance of gold and the nobility of its gemstone, and they said that it does not cause inflammation at the site of the incision, but this is not absolutely true.
I have found that this method works better in some bodies than others, and it is the best and most effective compared to iron, as they say. However, if you heat the needle in a gold fire, it will not be clear to you when it reaches the desired degree of redness for the gold.
And because it cools quickly, even if you increase the heat in the fire and melt it, it becomes brittle. Therefore, the use of iron is faster and more accurate for work, God willing.
And I have organized this chapter on cauterization into sections that I have arranged from the head to the foot, so that it will be easy for the student to find what he needs, God willing.
Chapter One.
For cauterizing the head, there is one method.
This method is beneficial for excess moisture and coldness in the brain, which are causes of headaches, excessive discharge from the head to the eyes and ears, excessive sleep, toothache, and earache. In summary, this method is effective for all diseases caused by coldness, such as paralysis, sciatica, and similar ailments.
This is a picture of that cyst, which orders the patient first to cleanse with a simple, pure medicine for the head three or four nights according to what necessitates the strength and habit of the patient.
Then he commands him to shave his head with a razor, and then sit before you with his hands on his chest.
Then place the base of your little finger on the base of his nose between his eyes, so that where your middle finger ends, mark that spot with a pen.
Then heat the olive oil lamp shown in this picture.
Uncover the bone as much as the head of a needle or the size of a poppy seed, then raise your hand and apply the hot iron or another if it has cooled down. Until you see the bone as I mentioned to you, then take some salt and dissolve it in water, and soak a cotton cloth in it and place it on the spot, leaving it for three days.
Then apply to it a cotton cloth soaked in oil and leave it until the scab from the fire disappears, then treat him with a quart of mercury until he is cured, God willing.
The wound, as long as it remains open, continues to drain pus, and that is better and more beneficial.
Some of them mentioned that the skin should be stretched over the bone and held until part of the bone marrow is burned; then, whatever has been burnt from the bone should be removed and treated afterwards.
Others said that it is necessary to stretch the skin until it affects the bone strongly, causing a small piece of bone, similar in size to a grain or a small nail head, to fall off. They claimed that this releases a vapor from that spot, and the wound should be left open for a long time.
Then it should be treated until it heals, and I do not see this type of stretching in most people except in some cases of gangrene. I prefer to leave it alone for safety reasons because the head will heal when its natural connection is separated, as we have observed in other parts of the body.
Especially if the patient's head is naturally weak, and I prefer the first type of stretching for it is safer and more effective. So use this method and may God grant you success.
Chapter Two.
Stretching the Skull as Well.
If there is a long and persistent pain in the head, and that is caused by an underlying condition, and treatments such as enemas, purgatives, baths, sweating, and bleeding were used, especially if he has previously used the single enema that we described, and it did not benefit him from that, look. If the patient's head is strong in nature and not weak, and he feels intense cold, then give him another enema on top of that one, but a little less. Then give him an enema on each forehead of his head until the coldness of the skin disappears and the extent of bone that we described is revealed. And give him an enema at the back of his head in the place known as the "behind the neck" and be gentle with your hand, do not expose the bone, for the patient will find this very painful, unlike the pain from the other head enemas, all of which I will mention in their places.
And the enema used for the forehead and back of the head should be milder than the enema used for the middle of the head, as we described it.
Chapter Three.
Cure the non-chronic sinus.
If pain occurs in the side of the head with swelling and the pain extends to the eye, the patient should be purged with cleansing medicines for the head, and the rest of the treatment that I mentioned in the classification of diseases should be used. If this does not cure it, then trepanation is performed on both sides. Either the trepanning with hot cautery, or with iron.
As for the trepanning with a hot cautery, it is done by taking one clove of garlic, peeling it and cutting off its edges from both sides. Then, make an incision in the painful spot of the cheekbone with a wide blade until there is a space under the skin to fit the clove.
It is placed under the skin until it disappears, then it is firmly bandaged with tight bandages and left for fifteen hours. Then it is unwrapped, and the garlic is removed, leaving the wound open for two or three days before dressing it.
And it is dressed with cotton soaked in oil until the spot heals. Then it is treated with poultices until it recovers, God willing. If you wish, you can do this with some of the burnt medicines that I mentioned in the eighteenth chapter on burnt medicines.
And as for cauterization with iron, it is done in this manner: the cautery, which is depicted here, is heated.
The cylindrical cautery is so called because its tip resembles a screw, and it has some indentations, with a small hole in the middle.
Then place it on the site of pain and hold it with your hand, gradually turning the iron little by little; thus, the amount burnt from the skin's thickness will be like half of it. And lift your hand so that you do not burn the veins below, which causes bleeding. Then drink cotton in salt water and place it on the site, leaving it for three days. Then carry the cotton with oil, then treat it with honey until it heals, God willing.
And if you wish, you can cut this incision with the smooth edge that comes from the cautery, and it will protect against cutting the veins in this incision except for the intended ones specifically.
Chapter Four.
Make a deliberate incision.
If you treated the incision with the remedies mentioned earlier and as described in the division of diseases, but the treatment did not work and you saw that there was no reason for it, then blame must be placed on the initial cauterization either with medication or fire. It is necessary that the surgical blade be heated until it becomes white after learning on the place of pain with a line length of half a finger or thereabouts, and leave your hand once and clamp it until the vein cuts and reaches near the bone.
Unless you avoid damaging the masticatory muscle, which moves during chewing, you will burn the nerve or motor muscle that activates it, causing paralysis.
Be cautious and careful not to rupture the vein you have cut, for there is danger in its cutting. Especially for those who are ignorant of what they do and are not experienced practitioners, it is best to leave the work to someone more skilled.
And the method of handling accidental rupture of a vein will be mentioned in its place in this book, God willing. If you see something that cannot be done with these methods, it is not your fault.
If you see the patient's body suitable for this method in the middle of the head as we described, then treat the wound until it heals, God willing.
And if you prefer, use the cauterizer we mentioned in the chapter on tying off veins with the double-bladed cautery, for it is a better and more effective method than this one.
The Fifth Chapter.
On the Pain of the Ears.
If pain occurs in the ear due to cold, and it is treated with compresses and other treatments mentioned in the division, but the pain does not go away, then use the cautery known as the point, which is shown here in its image.
Then, after heating it, use it to cauterize around the entire ear or both ears if the pain is in them. Keep the point away from the base of the ear slightly after learning its place by touch, and the point should be about ten points for each ear or thereabouts. Then treat the places until they are healed, God willing.
The Sixth Chapter.
On Weakness.
The weakness that is treated with cautery is of the type that occurs due to phlegm, as mentioned in the divisions of diseases.
And cautery should be avoided for the type that occurs due to dryness and nerve exhaustion.
If this type of weakness has been treated with ointments, suppositories, and potions, and the treatment did not work, it is necessary for the patient to be cauterized in three places. One at the base of the ear, the second a little below its root, and the third near the junction of the lips.

Chapter Eight.
The cure for forgetfulness.
The one who has ulcers should first drink from the large intestines and the clean brains for the brain.
Then his entire head should be shaved, and on the back of his neck, he should carry a pouch containing almonds written in the chapter on almonds, carrying it repeatedly for it is effective against ulcers.
And do this on the ribs themselves as mentioned above, for he will be cured by it; otherwise, make three fistulas in the back of his head, extending from the top of the head to the bottom of the neck.
And make the space between each fistula and the next one thick, like a finger, then treat the fistula as mentioned before. If you want to increase it and the patient can tolerate it, then open the middle fistula.
If you want to increase it, then open on the temples. Then treat him until he recovers, and the ulcer will be like an olive, as mentioned before.
Chapter Nine.
In the treatment of hernia and the healing of all parts of the body.
First, you should clean the head with vinegar and what we have mentioned. Then, shave the patient's head. Place a bandage in the middle of the head, and place a bandage on each side of the head, and another on the back.
And three on the neck, for if there is a need in healing the body to more than that and the patient can bear it, and the disease is strong and firm, then place four bandages on the sides of his back. And continue with the bandage until it burns most of his skin, then raise your hand and treat him as mentioned before until he recovers, God willing. The bandages should be made from olive oil.
Chapter Ten.
On bandaging the ulcer.
The ulcer that is to be bandaged, whose ulceration comes from the brain, should first have its head cleaned with large vinegar and all the treatment that we mentioned in the division. If the patient is big and can bear taking medicines, do so.
But if it is a child who cannot bear medicines, then use gargles and clean honey for the head several days before that, along with improving his diet.
Then he shaves his head, and cuts a single tuft of hair in the middle of the head as previously described, and another tuft at its rear. And on each horn of the head, a tuft; if the patient is strong and can withstand it, let him cut the tufts mentioned in the care of the parotid glands and on the neck and back, and the shaving should be olive-shaped as previously described.
If the patient is a child, make the shaving gentle in this manner.
The Eleventh Chapter.
In cutting of the tonsils.
If the cause of the tonsils is bad humors and thick phlegm, cut the tufts that we mentioned in the care of the parotid glands.
If the cause of the tonsils is a humoral imbalance leaning towards black bile, and the patient's body is moist, let him rinse his brain with what washes it as mentioned in the division [of diseases].
Then shave the patient's head, and make a firm cap from cotton like a circle, then place it in the middle of his head while the patient is sitting on his heels, holding each side. Then take one pound of old ewe's fat.
Then heat it over moderate fire as much as the finger can bear if placed in it, then pour it on his head within the circle and leave it until it cools down. Do this with the patient every week along with the rest of his good treatment until he is cured, God willing.
If you wish, let the poultice be small and numerous without your hand holding the bowl, but it should be a paste, for this type of poultice moistens the brain moderately.
Then place on it a cotton cloth soaked in oil or chicken fat.
Chapter Twelve
In the section on water poultice for the eyes.
If you notice the beginning of water in the eye with the signs mentioned in the classification, then hasten to wash the patient's head and keep him away from all moisture, and steam him in the bath on the steam for several days.
Then shave his head and apply a poultice in the middle of the head, then apply two poultices on the temples; if the water discharge starts in both eyes together or in one eye alone if it is in one eye.
Then cut with the scalpel all the veins and blood vessels beneath the skin, and let the sutures be in them in length according to the width of the jawbone, and take care not to spill the blood.
If you see anything of it, cut it off in place with any treatment that is possible for you, and we will come to the wisdom of closing the blood vessels and cutting them, and taking care not to spill [the blood].
And there may be in the heel under the bones two prominent sutures.
Chapter Thirteen.
On the suturing of chronic tears.
If the tear of the eye is chronic and persistent, and it is from the veins and blood vessels that are on the surface of the head outside the head, and you have confirmed that this is due to cold, thick, phlegmatic humors, then suture the tear as described with its eye at the beginning of the descending water.  (Note: The word "eye" here refers to a specific point or mark on the vein where the suturing should start.) A suture in the middle of the head, two sutures on the jaws, two sutures in the heel under the bones; and if it requires more, make a suture on each side of the tail of the eye on the edge of the eyelid with a small scalpel.
Chapter Fourteen
In the case of nasal polyps.
If you have treated it with what we mentioned in the division and the treatment does not help, then hurry to administer castor oil to the patient for three nights, then wash his head and cut the middle polyp with the olive oil probe. Then cut it with the screw probe two polyps above the eyebrows, under a little hair, and be careful not to cut the artery. This is the shape of the screw probe.
Chapter Fifteen
In the case of removing cataracts from the eye.
If the cataract of the eye is removed due to disease or moisture, cut one cataract polyp with this crescent probe.
And if you wish, cut two polyps above the eyebrows a little in each direction, and keep away from the eyelids, and let the length of each polyp be the length of the eyebrow.
Do not let your hand overdo the polyp, but only to the extent that it burns one-third of the skin, and this is the shape of the probe.
Chapter Sixteen
In the case of removing a cataract from the eye.
If its membrane has inverted inside, then press on the eye and cut it in two ways. And the cauterization, either by fire or by a burnt drug. As for cauterizing with fire, instruct the patient beforehand to remove his clothes if he is one who can undress until they become long and even.
So if its stem is short at the time of planting, tie his eyelids with a bandage so that they do not move until it grows. Once it has grown and settled, place the patient's head on your stone, then mark the corner of the eye with a pen in the shape of a leaf of asafoetida.
The beginning of the mark should be near the eye socket, then place a cotton swab soaked in egg white or azure blue under the eyelid and cover this swab with a patch.
Then cover the shape that you marked little by little in many times until the surface of the skin, which is like the leaf of asafoetida, is completely burned. The sign of your work being successful is that you see the eyelid has wrinkled and the hair has risen from the eye meat.
Lift your hand at that time and leave it for three days, then place a cotton swab with oil on it until the scabs fall off, then treat him with myrobalan until he recovers, if God wills. If any of the hair returns after a while and the eyelid wrinkles again.

Chapter Seventeen.
In the case of a sty on the eyelid.
If you treated the sty with what we mentioned in the section on diseases and it did not heal, then you must consider this feature.
The patient is instructed to place his head in your lap and to have a servant hold his head between your hands, ensuring that it does not move or shake.
Then place a soaked cotton cloth in the white of an egg or on the eyelids, and heat the cauterizing iron as shown in its image.
It should be hollow like the talon of an eagle, with one end closed and containing a hole. If you wish, you can make it open at both ends or even completely closed except that this hollow method is better for your work, if God wills.
Then, if it is open, squeeze out the pus from the nasal cavity and clean it. If it is not open, then open it and extract its contents, after which place the cauterizing iron on it, for it is very protective. Hold it with your hand until you reach the bone.  />
Then move your hand slightly towards the eye from the hole in the nasal cavity to avoid any error or causing anxiety to the patient, so that the cauterizing iron does not fall into the fat of the eye and damage it. If you reach the bone on the first try, good; otherwise, reheat the cauterizing iron a second time if needed.
Leave it for three days, then apply a flax cloth with oil and treat it with dried myrobalan until it heals. If forty days have passed and it has not healed, apply the sharp drug known as calcanthus until the bone is exposed. Then scrape it according to what will be mentioned in its chapter, God willing.

And pour into it the weight of a dirham of melted lead and hold the tube firmly with your hand so that the patient does not move, lest the melted lead flow into his eye. It is necessary to place a flax cloth on the patient's eye, dipped in egg white or water.
For lead burns the site of the ulcer and heals it wonderfully. If the ulcer does not heal with the methods mentioned for cauterization and treatment, then there is no choice but to pierce the nose and drain the ulcer into the nasal passage as will be detailed in its specific section.
Chapter Eighteen.
In the clefts of the lips.
It often happens that there are clefts in the lips, which are called hairs, especially in children's lips. If this cleft is treated as we mentioned in the division, and the treatment does not cure it, then a small hook-like knife should be used in this manner.
Its hollow should be on the blade of a knife, then place it in the cleft with a wheel until the hollow reaches the depth of the cleft, then treat it with cotton until it heals, God willing.
Chapter Nineteen.
On the Clefts of the Palate that Occur in the Mouth.
If it appears at the root of the gums, or on the palate, or at the roots of the teeth, and becomes inflamed, swells up, and bursts with pus, forming a cleft in the palate, then if treated, it does not heal. Therefore, one should apply a bandage that fits well into the cleft.
Then insert a bandage into the hole of the palate and grasp it with your hand until the iron is covered on both sides, and do this one or two times. After that, treat it as we have mentioned in the treatment until it heals, God willing.
If the bone is broken and clear, there is no need to uncover it; otherwise, it must be uncovered at the site, and the diseased bone should be removed according to what will come in its section, God willing.
The Twentieth Chapter.
On the treatment of carious teeth and rotten gums.
If the gums have rotted from moisture and the teeth have moved and were treated with drugs but did not improve, place the patient's head on a stone, then insert the probe into the tooth after placing the syringe on the tooth.
Then insert the hot syringe with the wheel, and hold your hand a little until the patient feels the heat of the fire reaching the root of the tooth; then lift your hand, then repeat the syringe several times according to what you want, then let the patient rinse his mouth with salt water.
And let him hold it for an hour, then spit it out; because the moving tooth will stabilize and the rotten gums will heal and the foul moisture will dry up.
The Twenty-First Chapter.
On the treatment of toothache.
If the toothache is from cold or there is a worm in it and does not improve with drug treatment, then treat it in two ways: either by cauterization with oil or by cauterization with fire.
The cumin with ghee is to take the cow's ghee and melt it in an iron pot or a frying pan, then take a piece of cotton and wrap it on the end of the reed, then dip it into the melted ghee and place it on the hurting tooth with a wheel, and hold it until it cools down.
Then repeat the process until the heat reaches the root of the tooth. If you wish, you can dip a wick or cotton in cold ghee and place it on the hurting tooth, and then cover it with a heated iron until the heat reaches the cavity of the tooth.
As for cauterizing with fire, it is done using a copper or iron tube, and there should be some thickness in the walls of the tube to prevent the heat of the fire from reaching the patient's mouth. Then heat the cap that matches its shape and place it on the same tooth, and hold your hand until the cap cools down. Do this several times.
The pain will disappear either that day or the next, and after this cauterization, it is necessary for the patient to fill their mouth with good ghee and hold it for an hour, then spit it out. This is what the cap looks like.
This is done on either side as desired and according to what is possible, and this is the appearance of the tube.
The Twenty-Second Chapter.
On Pig's Bladder.
If the pig's bladder is not ripe and free from cold humors, and has not been pickled with medicines for cooking, and you want to cook it quickly, heat an empty pot as shown in this image, both ends open.
Place the pot with the opening facing away from the bladder, and cover it twice if needed until it reaches the thickness of the bladder. If the bladder is small, adjust the size of the pot accordingly.
Then leave it for three days, and place a cotton cloth soaked in oil on top of it to absorb the smoke. After that, clean it with vinegar and water until it is purified, God willing.
The Twenty-Third Chapter.
On the Bladder for Hoarseness and Difficulty in Breathing.
If the humors have dominated the trachea, especially if this is accompanied by a cold temperament, it is necessary for the patient to first empty out with easy medicines, then insert a bladder into the incision at the base of the throat in the lower part.
Fear that it reaches the bones and do not burn more than half of the skin; then take another kay, at the joint of the neck in the last cartilage from it with a prominent hook, and the hook will be threaded as described before.
Then treat it with what was mentioned previously until it heals, if God wills.
The Twenty-Fourth Section.
In the kay, the disease of the ankle and the heel.
If the heel and ankle disease is due to cold moisture and there is no fever or inflammation, and if the disease is chronic, then take two kays above the ankles in the soft, empty places; also, take another kay in the middle of the chest between the breasts.
The hook will be threaded as described before, and if you wish, it may be a kay in which the hook is called al-naqta, and its figure has been shown previously in the treatment of earache, and the naqta will be from thirty naqtas to it.
Then treat it with what was mentioned before until it heals, and a three-pronged hook can be made on this figure, and the kay can be done quickly with it because you can take three kays with it in one time, and this is the figure of the hook.
Chapter Twenty-Five
In the chapter on hernias.
If the tendon's head slipped out due to wetness or was not properly secured when it returned from slipping, causing it to become accustomed to slipping and slip with the slightest movement as we have observed, then the jaw should be reset first. Then, the patient should lie on his back or on the healthy side, and the skin inside the hernia should be lifted up with the fingers of your left hand if the dislocation is towards the inside.
Then, heat the needle with two rods as shown in its image.
Then, use it to pierce the skin until the needle passes through to the other side. This forms a hernia with four openings. It can also be done with a needle having three grooves, making six openings at that time, and the grooves will be on the edge of the needle. بالتأكيد، لا تضيف ملاحظات أو تعليقات أو شرحات.

A good, screw-like cautery above the temple, or many cauteries that prick, for the joint will be strengthened and the moisture will go away, and the patient will recover.
Chapter Sixteen.
In cauterizing the stomach.
If cold and excessive moisture occurs in the stomach, altering its temperament and causing frequent urination, and it is not cured by usual treatments, then it is necessary to make the patient lie on his back, extend his leg and hand, and apply three cauteries. One cautery under the sternum to the extent of a finger with a screw-like iron, and two cauteries below it on each side of the single cautery so that they form a triangle, and keep them apart lest they join if inflamed; the depth of the cauterization should be one third the thickness of the skin, and such will be the shape of the cauteries.
According to this picture and in this measure, no more.
And if you wish, make one large cautery in the center of the stomach like this picture.
And the iron used for this single cautery should be in the shape of a circle like this picture.
He who fears this will cauterize the stomach with a point on it according to what is desired by pressure, then he will cauterize it with a pointed hook, and then he will treat it with the treatment that was mentioned until it heals.
The twenty-seventh section.
On cold cautery of the liver.
If the liver experiences pain due to cold or wetness, or due to a very strong wind that causes it to deviate from its natural humoral balance in an excessive manner, and if you treat the patient with what we mentioned in the classification, he will not benefit from this treatment. It is necessary for the patient to lie on his back and learn three cauteries in this manner and this amount, directly on the liver below the ribs where the human diaphragm ends.
And after each cautery, there should be another cautery the width of a thumb, and the cautery should be in a straight line along the body, and do not grip the hook tightly with your hand.
The amount of skin that should be burnt is half, no more, and the patient should stand on his feet; if he cannot stand, then let him lie down with his legs stretched out and his arms raised. And this is the shape of the hook.
And you can use a cautery iron for these wounds, if you have skill and caution in the craft, and be careful not to burn the skin completely so that it burns the abdomen and reaches the intestines, because the skin there is thin, so know that.
Chapter Twenty-Eight
In the case of an abscess and inflammation of the liver with a wound.
If there is a discharge from the liver and you want to know if that inflammation is in the flesh of the liver or in its capsule, for if it is in the flesh of the liver, then the patient will feel heavy and intense pain.
And if it is in the capsule of the liver, then there will be severe pain with limits, and you will see that the physicians have failed to treat it. Therefore, the patient should be made to sit on his heels, and then cauterize the warm area with a hot iron.
Then heat the cautery iron in the fire, and it is the iron that resembles a spear, and this is its shape. Cauterize the wound with it until the skin burns completely and the cautery reaches the capsule until all the discharge comes out, then treat it with the treatment for discharges until he recovers.
This type of cauterization should only be used by someone who has a long experience in the art of medicine and has treated these diseases by trial and error many times, for then he will excel in this work.
Chapter Twenty-Nine.
On Cauterizing the Nipple.
I mentioned earlier the cautery of the nipple by taking a long, dry root of the marshmallow plant, making it as thick as a finger, then soaking it in oil and lighting it in the fire. Then, place one cautery between the junction of the trachea and the neck, and two small cauteries slightly below the armpits slanted towards the side under the cheekbone, and two large cauteries on the chest between the third and fourth ribs.
Two more cauteries between the fifth and sixth ribs, slightly inclined towards the back, another in the middle of the chest, and one above the navel; three cauteries at the back: one between the shoulders, two beside the spine below the cautery that is between the palms;
It is not appropriate for your hand to be deep in the intestine, but it should be on the surface of the skin, barely touching. Some ancient authors mentioned that some people use an iron needle, similar to a spear, which they protect and insert between the ribs until it reaches the same worm.
The intestine comes out as we mentioned in the case of the liver worm, and in this case, there is danger that the patient may die from shock or that a lump appears at the site with no cure for it.
Chapter Thirty
The Cure of Wounds
If the treatment of the wound with what we mentioned in the division is not effective, then the cure for it is threefold, each one correct: One of them is to suture the wound with three or four stitches along its length.
Each stitch should be like the stitches of the liver, whose shape we have previously described. The distance between each stitch and the next should be about the thickness of a finger or slightly more. The thread used for the stitches should be the same type as mentioned for liver stitches. The patient's body should be laid flat on his back during this process, and your hand should not penetrate deeply into the wound.
The other side of the flap and lift the skin that is adjacent to the nipple, where the patient's flap ends, and lift the skin that is adjacent to the nipple on the left side, and your lifting of the skin should be across the body so that the sutures run along the length of the body.
Then, insert the needles very carefully until they emerge from the other side. Then remove the needle, leaving four sutures. If you wish to use another needle with three threads.
Then treat the sutured area after leaving it for many days, as it is better than any other treatment that has been presented before.
Chapter One and Thirty.
In suturing for incisions.
Suturing is only beneficial for narrow incisions, particularly if the patient has been treated with the methods of treatment we mentioned in the division, and your treatment did not help. Then it is necessary to suture four sutures around the wound and one suture on the stomach.
And another suture on the liver, and one on the nipple, and two behind his back between the ribs, one towards his chest and the other towards his stomach. The depth of the suture should be close to the thickness of the skin, then leave the suture open for a long time.
And do not neglect the patient after cupping, as he should be treated with what is appropriate to hasten his recovery. The shape of the cup used for cupping the back should be cylindrical, as shown in its picture, and the one used for cupping the side should be olive-shaped.
Chapter Two and Thirty.
On cupping the feet and calves.
If the feet and legs hurt and swell with yellow water, it is necessary to cup on top of the foot in the groove between the ankle and the heel.
And place your hand on the cup and do not move it, then raise your hand and do not repeat the process for a second time, as this will drain the yellow water, and the cup should be like this picture.
Then, on each leg, place two cups, one at the inner edge of the cup and one along the length of the leg, with one below the knee and another halfway down the leg, and on each thigh, also place two cups.
Leave the cup open without any treatment for a long time to allow water to drain from it, then treat it with everything else we mentioned.
Chapter Thirty-Three
Concerning hemorrhoids.
If the hemorrhoids are due to cold and moisture, which weakened the powers of digestion and retention in the stomach and intestines, and if this condition cannot be alleviated by various treatments, and you see that the patient is prone to hemorrhoids and has strong digestive power, then place a large clyster on his stomach. As described for the clyster of the stomach with a round enema, place four clysters around the anus to be inserted by means of a fine enema cane and a large cotton wad above the large intestine or two clysters.
If you see that moisture is abundant and the patient is prone to this, then place a clyster on the anus and a clyster on each hip, and perhaps two small clysters near the stomach, close to the large one. For it is a successful treatment whose benefit does not fail, God willing.
Chapter Thirty-Four
Concerning clysters for sitting patients.
If the patient is sitting for a long time, whether continuously or once, and if it is from thick, cold substances or bad moisture, and if you treated him according to what we mentioned in the division, then the treatment did not benefit. So place three clysters on the lower part of the back, under the ribs, slightly triangular.

In the incision of the nose

If it extends to the thigh and shin, then make two hooks on the thigh in the place indicated by the patient's pain. Make a hook above the ankle, four fingers towards the heel side, slightly shallow. The knife should be like a sword, and the depth of the hook should be equal to only the skin's fat.
If the pain extends towards the fingers of the foot, then make a small incision where indicated with a pointed knife three or four times, or more if needed. And if the pain is below the ankle towards the shin, then make one sword-like incision there.
And be careful in all incisions that the hook does not reach to burn a large nerve or vessel, for this will cause the patient severe pain or prolonged recovery.

From the salt of the sea and from unslaked lime, take an equal part of each, grind them together and place them in a new pot with a small hole at its base to allow the solution to flow out. Underneath this pot, place another smaller vessel.
And pour cold water on the sea salt and lime, enough to cover them, then knead with your hand until well mixed. Leave the pot until the liquid flows into the smaller vessel beneath it. Then collect all that liquid, pour it onto fresh lime and new sea salt, and repeat the process.
For it becomes then very strong, used in many medical procedures and for various body parts because it behaves like fire itself. Among the medicines that also work with it are those made from althea, honeycomb, lime with soap, both well prepared.
And Galen tells a story of an ancient man who cured the pain of gout and sciatica, considering it highly effective and claiming that no other treatment is needed, as it can cure in one application.
To the point that sometimes he would enter the bathhouse carrying it and leave cured, which is to take green nettle; if green is not available, then newly dried nettle is taken, its powder mixed with a little oil, and applied to the gout in the foot or leg or thigh.
It is cauterized and left for three hours or as long as the patient feels the burn, then he enters the bath. If his body swells, he should enter the pool, for the pain will subside and he will heal with God's permission. If he does not heal, the cautery is repeated after ten days.
For he will heal, God willing. Know that no one should use these medicines except after purging the body. Dioscorides mentioned that the cautery of the labia minora, if performed with the juice of the nettle, is beneficial.
The cautery is performed in this manner: take a woolen thread, dip it in old oil, and place it on the deep spot between the thumb and the index finger, closer to the index finger. Then take a dried nettle leaf.
Then light it with fire until it becomes a coal, then place it on the wool and let it cool. Then take another one and continue doing this until the feeling reaches the middle of the finger and the pain subsides by God's will. This type of cautery is called "the nettle cautery.
Chapter Twenty-Four.
In pain in the back
It may present as pain in the back due to many causes, such as a fall, a blow, or excessive exertion, and the like. And it is characterized by cold, moist matter.
For that which is due to the accumulation of cold matter, it is necessary after the patient's exertion and similar actions that he should lie on his back where the pain is, in three rows the same width as a tablecloth, after learning the place with kneading in each row five handfuls or more according to what you see of the patient's strength and endurance.
And the kneading should be with a circular motion, and if you wish, you can knead it three or four times with an average-sized spindle in this manner.

On the onset of sciatica

Chapter Forty-Four
On the threading of hernias and joint pains.

And if it is necessary to bandage the face of the foot, do so with a point bandage. If the pains rise to the ankles or to other joints, which often happens, cover each ankle with three or four threads from each side using this olive-colored bandage.

The Fifty-Fourth Chapter.
On the Incision of the Fistula.
If a fistula appears in the anus, and some of the excrement and feces discharge to the outer surface, and this happens at first close by, it is necessary that the patient be ordered to fast for one day and to use among the laxatives what will help expel the pus from his body.
Then he should lie on his back in front of you, and you order him to hold his breath until the feces or excrement protrudes. Then press it back with your finger, then make a mark below the fistula under the anus on the bone of the coccyx in the shape resembling half a circle, its edges pointing upwards towards the body.
Then you cover this vessel with its own skin.
until it comes out white, removing the dirt, then return the urine or pus to its cavity; then place an assistant's hand on the spot so that the urine does not emerge, and I have made an incision between the patient's thighs and placed a pad beneath it, and another assistant binds his thigh.

The Sixty-Fourth Section
In the hole of the awl.

Chapter Forty-Eight.

Chapter Ninety-Four
In the case of a swelling.
If the swelling advances and does not respond to any of the remedies of medicine, then cut a small incision in it until the whiteness disappears and its color changes.
Then treat it with lentil flour mixed with mallow leaf extract, swallowwort juice, and pigeon blood or blood of the white-crowned sparrow, each in equal parts, mixing all together and applying on a bandage, securing the place until it heals.
Chapter Fifty
In the case of cancer.
If the cancer is in its early stages and you wish to contain it, cut around it with a circular incision as it grows. Some wise men have said to make a deep incision in the middle of it, but I do not see this as beneficial because I expect that it will ulcerate, and I have witnessed this happening multiple times.
The correct way is to incise around it with a circle as we have said, or with many small incisions.
Chapter Fifty-One.
In the treatment of the uvula.
If any of the uvula is delayed in healing, whether due to the insufficient strength of its nutrient or due to the patient being old with little blood, or due to the passage of time and you intend to hasten the healing of the uvula, then incise around it with many small incisions.
Then leave it, for it will hasten in healing. If you want to cauterize with a hot iron, heat the cautery as shown in this figure.
And lower it into the middle of the uvula until the skin is burned, and let the incision be from above downward to facilitate the flow of pus. Then treat it with what is appropriate until it heals.
Chapter Fifty-Two.
In the treatment of hernia.
The hernia is nothing but a decay that strives to consume the limb, just as fire consumes dry wood. If you see a hernia in a place suitable for cauterization with fire, heat numerous fine and coarse needles, according to what suits that place where the hernia is located.
Then, clean it from every side until all the corruption is removed and nothing remains of the pus; then leave it for three days, and apply powdered sulfur with oil on the affected areas until all the scabs come off along with all the corruption.
Then treat it with the growing meat cauteries, for if after three days you see that the flesh grows healthily without corruption, then continue [the treatment]. Otherwise, repeat the cautery on what remains of the corrupted areas, and sometimes the ulcer can be treated with strong medicine.
For it takes the place of fire, and is more effective. I have mentioned its treatment with strong medicine in the division, so take it from there when you need it.
Chapter Thirty-Five.
On the cautery of the inverted and non-inverted nipples.
It often happens in the soles of the feet; it is a hard thing that pains the man, and there are two ways to cauterize it: either by fire or by strong water.
As for the cautery by fire, it is done with a wide, hollow metal probe, shaped like an eagle's claw, made to fit around the nipple on all sides and very thin in its edges. Then, heat the probe until it becomes hot enough, then place it on the nipple and rotate your hand with the probe around the nipple until the probe reaches the depth of the nipple.
"Leave it for three days, wrapped in the rind of a salted country loaf, and leave the wrap on overnight, as it will detach from its base. Then treat the wound site with a poultice prepared from meat until it heals, if the stitches are not inverted.
"And often it occurs on the surface of the body, especially in the hands and feet. Therefore, you should take a tube made of copper or iron or an eagle's quill and place it over the stitch or thread, then pour some boiling water into the tube.
"And hold the tube with your hand, turning it slightly with your hand so that the edge of the tube affects the base of the stitch and the boiling water finds its way to the base of the stitch. The patient should endure the heat of the boiling water for an hour.
"Then leave it, for the stitch will detach from its base. Do this one by one until you have done so with all of them in the body. Then treat their places after they have detached with a poultice prepared from meat.
The Fourth and Fiftieth Chapter
In the case of hemorrhage.
If a person experiences hemorrhage from cold in the nerves, or from the heat of fever, or any other cause, it is necessary to apply four or five poultices on the spine between each vertebra and one on the chest. And on his abdomen, a poultice with olive oil, for the hemorrhage will subside and the cold disease will heal quickly.
The Fifth and Fiftieth Chapter.
In the case of a rupture occurring in the body.
If there is a rupture in the body, which is ugly and caused by cold, thick, and foul matter, it is necessary that at the first appearance of the wound, a light poultice should be applied to the top of each rupture with ashes burned at the end with fire or with the root of long reeds or with lentil oil.
A light poultice should be applied in this manner to hemorrhoids at their first appearance, and they will not increase or become inflamed again, but the patient will recover from them unless the patient is purged beforehand.
The Sixth and Fiftieth Chapter
In the treatment of wounds resulting from the cutting of veins.
It often happens that a wound in a cut vein exposes blood that is difficult to stop bleeding.
If this happens to someone, hurry with your hand to the mouth of the vein and place your little finger on it and squeeze it firmly until the blood is confined under your finger and nothing comes out of it. Then put in the fire small and large olive pits, many of them, and blow on them until they become very hot.
Then take one of them, either small or large, according to the size and location of the wound where the vein was cut, and place the hot pit on the same spot after removing your finger quickly, and hold the pit until the bleeding stops.
If the bleeding resumes when you lift your finger from the mouth of the vein and the pit cools down, quickly take another hot pit from the prepared pits in the fire, and continue to do this with one after another until the bleeding stops.
And be careful not to burn a nerve, as this will cause the patient another illness. Know that if the vein is cut and bleeding, it cannot be stopped, especially if the vein is large, except by one of four methods: either by cautery, as we have mentioned, or by ligature if it has not already been tied off. If the bleeding is reduced at its end and the blood flow is cut off, either a secure and firm ligature can be tied with threads, or medicines that stop bleeding and constrict with bandages firmly can be applied to it.
And if someone tries to stop it by ligature or constricting with cloth, or applying burnt substances and the like, it rarely stops the bleeding that way. If this happens to anyone and he is without a doctor or medicine, let him quickly place his forefinger on the mouth of the wound itself, as we have described.
He should press it very hard until the blood is constrained and it freezes over the wound, on the artery and the finger, and water should not be poured onto it. The cold water should always be very cold, so that the blood congeals and thickens and stops. During this time, he should look for what he needs from a lancet or medicine.
Chapter Two.
In incisions, lacerations, fistulas, and other wounds.
It was said by Khalf, as we mentioned in the first chapter, that for every disease where cautery with fire and burnt medicines is beneficial, there are causes and tools, and images of the moxibustion process have been made, and I have considered all this from the crown to the sole.
And I have threaded this chapter with that thread, so as to facilitate for the student what is required.
Before I begin, it is important for you to know, my children, that this chapter has more errors than the first chapter on the knee.
And for this reason, the warning in it must be severe, as working in this chapter often leads to the loss of blood, which is the essence of life, through opening a vein or an artery, treating a wound or removing a bullet or arrowhead, or incising over a stone, and similar things that all carry risk and fear, and death occurs in most of them.
And I advise you to avoid what is ambiguous for you, for in this craft you will encounter people of various diseases, some of whom have been weakened by their illness and death has drawn near to them.
Because of the severity of his illness, the length of his affliction, and how resigned he is to his condition as a sign of approaching death, some people will spend their wealth on you in hopes of regaining health, even though their illness is terminal. You should not assist those who come to you with these characteristics. ان البيت هو مكان الخلوة والسرور، يجب أن يتماشى فيه السعد والسراء، ويقلع الغم والحزن. فإذا كان بيتك مليئً بالسراء، يجب أن يكون الطبيب مليئً بالسعد.
And let your caution be greater than your desire and effort, and do not proceed with any of that until after certain knowledge that confirms the praiseworthy outcome for you. Use in all treatment of your diseases the advancement of knowledge and warning about what tends toward safety.
For in that you have aid in attaining praise and glory, remembrance and thanks, may God guide you, my sons, to right guidance and not deny you the correct path and success, for that is in His hands; there is no god but Him.
And this chapter has been divided into sections, as was done in the chapter on wounds from the foot to the neck, so that you may understand what you seek from it, God willing.
The first section.
In the treatment of water that collects in the heads of children.
Indeed, this disease often afflicts children at birth if the midwife presses the child's head roughly, and it may also be caused by a hidden cause that is not known.
And I have not seen this cause in anyone other than children, and all those whom I saw of them died quickly for this reason. Therefore, I did not treat it, and indeed I saw among them a child whose head had become filled with water and the head became swollen every day. Until the boy does not sit on himself for the swelling of his head, and the moisture increases until he dies.
And this moisture, either accumulates between the skin and the bone, or it accumulates under the bone on the brain, and to treat this if the moisture is between the skin and the bone, and the worm [swelling] is small, it is necessary to make a single incision in the middle of the head, its width should be one finger and its length about two fingers until the moisture drains. This is the image of the trepanned [patient].
If the moisture is greater and the swelling is larger, then make two intersecting incisions like this image:
And if the moisture is under the bone, and its sign is that you see the sutures of the head open from all sides, and water descends when you press it with your hand, and this is not hidden from you, then it is necessary to make three incisions in the middle of the head like this image.
After the incisions, all of the moisture will exit. Then close the incisions with sutures and bandages. Then apply a mixture of drink and oil to them for five days. After that, remove the bandages and treat the wound with linen and wine compresses. Do not leave the head tightly bandaged. And feed the patient with all dry foods that have little moisture.
To the point where the limb becomes strong and heals, another method of excision is to look for where the bone of the tumor and the collection of water appear, because it may be more in the back of the head or in its front or on the right or on the left.
You aim to excise where the tumor and the water collection appear, so excise it as much as you can, being careful not to cut a vessel which would cause suppuration that could kill the patient from that suppuration along with the moisture.
Chapter Two.
Cutting the vessels behind the known auditory bones.
When someone experiences severe headaches that affect the eyes or the chest, and this condition persists even after trying medical treatments, then the treatment for it is to cut these two vessels.
If you wish to cut them, you should first shave the head of the patient with a razor, then probe the place with a rough needle so that the vessels appear; then tie the neck of the patient with his cloth, observe where the pulse beats and their location, which are two low places behind the ears, for they are not hidden except in some people.
Then learn on them with the saw, then cut them with the lancet to the bone, and that will be by the width of the head. And if you wish, insert the lancet from below the jaw and drive it upwards with the cut, and the length of the cut will be about two fingers.
If the artery is cut, blood will gush out in pulsating spurts, flowing forward and backward continuously. If the jawbone does not appear to be visible, it should be estimated from the ear by three fingers' length, then learn with the saw and bore to the bone.
Blood clots form on the midline, and sometimes more or less is sent out, all depending on the strength of the patient and the fullness of his blood vessels. Then look at the wound; if any part of the shaving remains on the bone, cut it off.
So that it does not expose a hot wound, then suture the wound with a thread of linen cloth, and treat it with bandages until it heals.
Chapter Three.
Excise the jaws that are in the mouth.
If a person has chronic or severe toothache, inflammation in the muscles of the jaw, or similar conditions, and they are not cured by the usual medical treatments, we have tried in these diseases to excise the jaws from the mouth or cauterize them as described.
The approach to treat it is for the patient to shave the hair on the temples, aiming for the visible vein in the temple, as its pulse is clearly discernible, and little remains hidden except in exceptional cases among individuals.
Or, if the cold is severe and it is hidden from you, let the patient wrap his neck with a cloth, then pierce or apply hot water to the spot until the vein appears clearly and distinctly. Then take the lancet that looks like this. Then cut the skin with it until you reach the vein, then insert a thread into it and pull it upwards until it exits the skin. Clean it of any impurities on both sides. If the vein is thin, moisten it with the end of the thread. Then cut a piece from it, the length of which is determined by how much it will retract and contract without causing bleeding. For if it does not burst or break, no blood will flow at all. Then let the blood drain for six to three cups.
If the vein is large, it should be tied in two places with a strong double thread, either of linen or made from the strings of a lute, so that gangrene does not set in before the wound heals and cause bleeding.
