The Seventh and Eightieth Chapter
On Cutting Limbs and Bone Exposure.
If the limbs are putrefied, whether from an external or internal cause, and if treatment with medicines does not cure it and you see that the corruption is advancing in the member and nothing stops it,
Then it is necessary to cut that limb until the corruption reaches, in order to save the patient from death or great affliction which is worse than losing the limb. A sign of its need for amputation is when the member becomes blackened to such an extent that you think fire has burnt it.
Or if it putrefies after blackening, to the point that this corruption extends beyond that member and affects the rest of the body, then hasten to cut it off. Similarly, if the cause of the putrefaction is due to a venomous creature such as a sea scorpion, a snake, or a scorpion, and the like.
If the putrefaction or venom is in the tip of the finger, then cut off the finger and do not delay the amputation until the putrefaction spreads to the hand. Similarly, if it affects the hand, cut it off from its root at the wrist and do not delay the amputation until it spreads to the forearm.
And so if he took in the arm, cut off the arm at the joint itself, and if there was gangrene and you saw it reaching towards the shoulder, do not cut off the shoulder, for that would cause the patient to die; use another treatment according to your ability.
Likewise, if gangrene occurs in the toe, cut off the toe at one of its joints. And if it occurs in the foot, cut off the foot at its ankle. If it reaches the leg, cut off the leg at the knee joint.
And if the gangrene has reached above the knee, there is no remedy except to leave it and let the patient die. The method of cutting off a limb or removing it is to bind a ligature below the place you wish to cut and bind another ligature above the place.
And the attendant who holds the lower ligature should pull it downwards, and another attendant holding the upper ligature should pull it upwards, and you should scrape off the flesh between the two ligatures with a broad scalpel until all the flesh is exposed, then cut or remove it. It is necessary to place bandages of linen on all sides.
So that the saw does not touch the correct place and cause the patient excessive pain and burning, if bleeding occurs during your work, quickly cover the place or apply some astringents to stop the blood, then return to your treatment until you finish.
Then, attach the wounded limb with a suitable bandage and treat it until it heals. I inform you of an example of a man with a wound in his leg. This affliction is similar to what I have described for you, for it happened in his leg as a dark mark accompanied by a burn that resembles fire.
And that corruption first occurred in his finger, until it spread to the entire leg. When the man saw the corruption spreading through the limb along with the intensity of the pain and burning sensation, he amputated it at the joint, and was cured.
After a long time had passed, that same corruption appeared in his little finger. He sought me out and I cut off that finger using the medicines I placed on his hand after cleansing his body. But the corruption did not leave and spread to the next finger.
Until the corruption reached his hand, he called for me to cut off his hand. I refused and urged him to reattach that finger, fearing his death upon cutting off his hand since the man was in a weak state. When he gave up hope of this, he returned to his homeland.
I was informed that he later had his hand amputated and recovered. I have told this story so that it may serve as an aid in dealing with cases of this disease, and to be a guide to act upon.
Chapter Eighty-Eight
On the treatment of abscesses and how to inject them with medicines.
If a worm appears in one of the fleshy members and its duration is prolonged until it reaches the maximum length, then it either bursts or ruptures and all that was inside it comes out, leaving the place empty as if it were a vessel.
And the skin over it is like a membrane and has not yet been deeply affected by decay, so that it does not affect bone or nerve or ligament. From here it deserves to be called an abscess, and it is not named "nasura" unless its duration lengthens until the decay affects something of these members.
Then it is called "nasura" or "zikama". Its treatment is to cut off all that skin as if it were peeling, especially if it has thinned and become like a membrane and is sure not to adhere to the place because of its decay.
If it is hoped that the skin will adhere and its decay has not reached that extent, and there is some flesh in the skin, then treat it with an injection. This is done by looking at the abscess; if it is large and the tip of the swelling from which the odor emanates is prominent, then inject it with the Egyptian drug. باسم الله.
The one that is mixed with oil, honey, and a vinegar solution in equal parts, gathered in a container and cooked over fire until the medicine boils and reaches the consistency of honey. Then take from it what you need and dilute it with water and honey, and inject it into the wound, close his mouth, and leave the medicine in it for two hours.
Then remove it during the afternoon, doing this daily until the wound is clean and the pus is gone. If you do not have this medicine, inject water with ash from the trunk of a carob tree or the trunk of an olive tree, mixed with water.
Then strain it and inject until you are sure the wound is clean. If the patient cannot tolerate Egyptian medicine or ash water, then inject with water and honey mixed with some powdered vinegar.
Or inject with a mixture of honey and wine, for it is the nature of honey to cleanse and wash, while wine closes the wound, especially if it contains a little rosemary or sage. Do this several times until you are sure that the corruption has left the wound, then inject with something that promotes flesh growth.
Like taking the date stone and coating it with rose oil and astringent drink, or injecting it with some medicines and other pits that we have proven their properties in the chapter on pits, for if the mouth of the hidden one is narrow and does not fit the injection tube.
Then widen it slightly with iron, or put a swab in it soaked in Egyptian pits or pits of the Syrians until it expands. And if the mouth is also wide, gather its lips with stitching and leave as much as needed to fit the injector without excess.
Likewise, if the mouth from which the pus is draining is elevated above the fissure, cut it lower in a deeper place so that the pus flows downward, because if the pus is injected into the bottom of the hidden place, it prevents the flesh from growing therein.
If you cannot cut the hidden place downward as desired, crush and apply a poultice that easily drains pus from it according to what seems best to you, and crush so that nothing of the stubborn pus remains in it.
As for the medicines that are placed on the hidden place from outside and how to apply them, it is to take one of the suitable medicated pits according to what you want, and spread it on a cloth made of cotton. And let the cloth be as much as needed to cover all of the hidden place. Then, you carve with the scissors a wider hole than the mouth of the cavity slightly. Then, you put on it a soft bandage over another bandage to match the size of the hole and place it away from the mouth of the cavity so that it is easy for the pus to come out, and do not remove the large bandage except later.
Several days, and the one over the mouth of the cavity is the one that you remove at all times so that what has accumulated in it can come out and to know what comes out of it: whether it is a lot or a little, or purulent or non-purulent.
With this, you also examine the same place of the cavity: Does the person feel pain in it or not? Is there a worm or no worm? If your treatment continues like this and you see the matter coming out smoothly from the mouth of the cavity.
Know that the cavity has healed or is close to healing, so at that time you should open it again on the next day or on the third day. When the wound opens, replace the bandage with another one and renew the dressing. If after a long period thin pus comes out of the cavity, do not despair from its healing.
He delays in the formation of flesh in his wound, and some are opposite to that, so if he comes out of the store after many days without inflammation, know that the store has not adhered, for delaying the adhesion of the store is a sign of health.
And his condition worsened, so he increased in the drying of the medicines, and let the medicine be in its composition wet and in its strength dry, like a dried date if it has been increased with more sugar, and whoever reaches the point that what he treats with is to take the dried date.
And he is anointed with rose oil and sprinkled on him the old balanced drink in its composition, then it is kneaded with it and used, and this action can be done if dried dates are not available, if honey is cooked until it boils and used, or take of raisins, figs, and cardamom and crush all and leave them on the honey while it is on the fire. Then it is poured on a cloth and applied to the wound, or it can be poured with honey that has been cooked until it thickens, and the shells are placed on it, then the cloth is put on and secured.
And it can be used in such cases, long strips of the root of the safflower and powdered poppy seeds and the individual peels of quinces are employed, either alone or ground up together, sifted and left on honey that has been described and used. If the matter of the wound persists and does not heal with this treatment, know that there is corruption within it.
And it has an effect on the bones or other hard tissues and ligaments, so treat it with Nasor treatment as described previously.
Chapter Ninety-Eight.
In the treatment of fistulas, ingrown toenails, excess fingers, and finger joint dislocation.
A fistula is an excessive growth of flesh that develops under the toenail of the hand or foot, and sometimes in other fingers. If its condition persists and treatment is neglected, it will become inflamed and painful.
Or it may become corrupt and gangrenous, eventually eating away at the root of the nail, sometimes corrupting the entire nail, and sometimes reaching the bone so that it gives off a foul odor, and the tip of the finger becomes swollen and its color changes to blackish. If you treat it with what we mentioned in the section and it does not heal, your treatment has failed.
It is necessary to cut with iron all the flesh that grows from the nail, then dress the wound after that, for cauterization in this case is very beneficial. As for if the bone is intact and the nail is also intact.
The corner of the nail has sunk into the flesh, causing ulceration and inflammation. It is necessary to place a thin piece of wood under the corner of the nail that sinks into the flesh, lift it up, and cut off that piece of flesh with pincers.
And on what remains of the flesh, place burnt medicines that are not too strong until it all disappears, then treat it with poultices until it heals. But if the infection has affected the bone, it is necessary to cut out that bone and remove it, for it will not heal as long as there is a rotten piece of bone in it.
If you see corruption and putrefaction advancing in the finger, cut it off at one of the joints as mentioned before, then treat (the stump) until it heals. If the nail is struck or crushed and severe pain occurs, it is necessary to first lance the affected area.
Then, cut the nail with a sharp knife, making a slanted cut from top to bottom. Be careful not to let the cut reach the flesh under the nail, for this will cause severe pain to the patient and may result in excessive flesh growth in that area. Then, treat the site with what soothes the pains.
And as for the extra finger that is born in some people's hands, sometimes it is all fleshy and sometimes there are bones in some of them, and sometimes there is a nail. Its root may be connected to some of the fingers.
Or its root may be in some part of the finger, and that which grows from some part of the finger does not move. However, that which grows near the base of the finger might move, and whatever is fleshy, it can easily be cut off, and this is done by cutting it at its base with a wide blade.
As for the one whose root is at the base of the joint, its treatment is difficult because it tends to recur after being cut off. And as for the one that grows on the finger near one of the joints, it is preferable to first cut its flesh in a circular manner to the bone, then saw the bone with one of those appropriate saws.
Then treat it until it heals. And as for the adhesion that occurs between some of the fingers, this is often seen and is one of the things with which humans are born. It may occur during the union of a wound or burn, and similar cases. In such instances, it is necessary to cut open that adhesion.
Until the fingers return to their natural state, then place between them a bandage or gauze soaked in rose oil so that it does not stick quickly and separates between them, or make between them a thin lead sheet until the place is healed as needed.
And likewise, if there is adhesion of some fingers with the palm, break that adhesion according to what can be prepared and adjusted for the shape of the limb.
Chapter Ninety-Nine.
On Cutting Nails.
Nails are thick, rough, blackish veins that occur in most parts of the body but are most common in the legs and particularly among those who walk a lot, such as porters and travelers. It is necessary first to use powerful bleeding from the body, repeated several times.
Then the owner of the nail should use cautery, and as for its treatment with iron, it will be on two strikes: one to break open and release the black blood, and the other to scrape away the vein and remove it entirely. As for breaking it open, this is done by first scalding the leg with very hot water.
Until the thick blood clot dissolves, tie the patient's leg above his thigh to below his foot with a bandage, then make an incision in one place or two places or three wide incisions.
Then remove the black blood with your hand from below the leg to above and from above to below until you extract a sufficient amount of blood, or as much as the patient's strength allows. Then bind it and order him to avoid foods that cause constipation. Repeat the bleeding and purging.
When the veins fill up and cause harm to the patient, but if he sweats, it will be of this kind: shave the patient's leg if it has a lot of hair, then have him enter the bath and wash his leg with hot water until it becomes red and the vein swells or he performs intense exercise.
If there is no bath to heat the limb, then make a longitudinal incision in the skin along the vein, either at its end near the ankle or below it near the heel. Then open the skin with scissors and clean the vein from both sides until it becomes visible.
He appears red and swollen upon emergence, and if freed from the skin, he also resembles a leech. Then, inserting a reed under him until it rises above the skin, secure it with a thin, soft thread, then make another incision near that one, about three fingers wide.
Then, scrape the skin from above the vein until it appears. Raise it with a reed as you did before and secure it with another thread as you did initially. Then, make one more incision or several incisions if necessary.
Then, tie it off and cut it at the end of the incision near the knuckle. Draw it out, tie it off until it exits the second incision. Draw it to the upper incision and do that until you draw it from the highest of all incisions. Once it is all drawn out, cut it.
If you find it difficult to pull and tie, insert a two-pronged needle with a strong thread. Tie it off and pull the needle out while sliding a reed under it. Move your hand in all directions until it exits. Make sure it does not break, because if it breaks, it will be very hard to tie off.
The afflicted person will suffer from it, so if he has a wound, place on the location of the wound moist wool in vinegar and rose oil or olive oil and treat him until he recovers. If the wound is swollen with convulsions, it tends to turn towards various directions.
And if it is not upright as we mentioned, then it must be cut at every angle and place of its convulsions, then attach it with ligatures until all are gathered together. Be careful when cutting it not to cut the vein or wound it, for that would make it difficult for you to gather, so protect your effort.

Chapter One Hundred Nineteen.

Chapter 39.
On making an incision in the disease known as elephantiasis.
This disease that is called elephantiasis in our country is a pain that appears in some limbs, then moves from one limb to another, and I have seen it as I described it to you.
I was called to a sick woman in one of the villages, and when she uncovered her arm, I found an inflammation that had entered into the vein of her arm. After an hour, I saw that inflammation rising with the blood, just like the beetle ascending, quickly reaching the armpit as fast as possible, like mercury.
If you move from one place to another, the pain leaves that place and settles in the armpit. Then, after an hour, it spreads throughout the body until it reaches the other arm. After that, she told me that her whole body was turning as I witnessed.
I was amazed at the speed with which the disease spread from limb to limb, and I had never seen this illness before in such a form except that I had seen a group who found pain spreading from limb to limb, but I did not see it as I saw it in this woman.
I could only attribute this to the fact that the woman was from the countryside, with a dry and exposed body. Thus, the moving wind could be perceived more easily, and it would not appear in this manner among city dwellers with moist and hidden bodies.
If you intend to treat it and the patient feels pain, then if it appears as described, tighten above and below it with a tourniquet, and cut until that trapped wind is released and the place heals.
If you do not see it, then treat it by inducing vomiting and using remedies that expel winds, such as mint seeds, caraway seeds, and similar drugs.
Chapter Forty-Nine.
On Extracting Arrows.
Arrows differ according to their types and the parts of the body in which they are embedded. As for their variations in type, some are large while others are small; some have hollow glass tips, others solid glass tips, and some have three or four barbs.
Some have tongues, others have feathers; and as for the parts of the body in which they are embedded, they fall into two categories: either the affected part is a hollow organ such as the brain, heart, liver, lungs, kidneys, bladder, intestines, and similar organs. When an arrow strikes one of these hollow organs and the signs of imminent death that I have described to you appear, it is best not to remove the arrow from such a place, for death will likely overtake its bearer. When these ugly signs do not appear and the arrow is not stuck in the hollow of the limb, then take it out and treat the wound. The signs of brain injury are: if an arrow pierces the bone and wounds the soft part on top of the brain, a severe headache and vertigo result from this.
When these ugly signs do not appear and the arrow is not stuck in the hollow of the limb, then take it out and treat the wound. The signs of brain injury are: if an arrow pierces the bone and wounds the soft part on top of the brain, a severe headache and vertigo result from this. There is redness in the eyes, redness of the tongue, dizziness, confusion, one episode of vomiting, and sometimes blood comes out from the nostrils or ears. Sometimes speech is lost and hearing goes away. From the place of the wound, a white, watery discharge like pus comes out, resembling meat in its consistency.
If these signs appear to you, then refrain from treating the patient and removing the arrow if it has not already been removed. As for the signs of an arrow wound: if the heart is pierced and it is near the left shoulder and you can feel that it is lodged in something hard, not in something hollow.
And sometimes the arrow has a pulsation like the pulse, and black blood flows from the wound, followed by coldness in the extremities, cold sweat, and pallor. Know that death is imminent. The sign of an arrow wound if it injures the liver is the effusion of thick blood from the wound.
The thyroid that is below the neck becomes swollen, and the patient's color changes, and they breathe deeply and seek cold air to inhale. If the arrowhead has reached the diaphragm, it will be close to the small ribs, and breathing will be severe with intense pain.
The patient becomes restless, and all the limbs of the afflicted side move. If the arrow has reached the liver, this will be followed by severe pain, and blood resembling the liver in its redness will flow from the wound. If the arrow has reached the intestines, food may sometimes come out undigested.
The patient's condition is evident. If the arrow has reached the abdomen and exited, something from the intestines or bladder may come out of the wound, such as pus or a broken vessel. There is no hope for treatment or removal of the arrow. If the arrow has reached the bladder, urine will flow out.
Something will protrude from the wound, and pain will intensify for the patient, indicating that they have died. As for the rest of the body parts such as the face, eye, ear, shoulder, arm, and similar parts, it is generally accepted.
When the arrow did not encounter a vein or nerve, and was not poisoned, I will inform you of some observations regarding these arrows to aid in your treatment. For instance, an arrow fell into a man's eye socket at the root of his nose.
I extracted it from the other side, under the temple of his ear, and he was cured with no adverse effects on his eye. I also removed another arrow for a Jew that had struck him in the socket of his eye beneath the lower eyebrow. It had barbs, so I split it between the bones and since it had pierced his cheek, I handled it carefully until I extracted it. The Nasranite recovered and was cured. I also removed another arrow for a man who had been struck in the abdomen; we thought he would die from it.
When he remained for thirty days or thereabout, and nothing changed in his condition, the arrowhead broke and became dislocated on him, and it was extracted, and he recovered without any unfortunate event occurring to him. And I saw a man whose arrow fell into his back, so the wound closed on him.
After seven years, the arrow came out at the base of his thigh. And I saw a woman who had an arrow fall into her abdomen, and the wound closed on her, leaving the arrow inside; nothing changed in her condition, nor did she find any harm in any of her natural functions.
I saw another man who had an arrow fall into his face, and the wound closed on him, leaving little pain. And many are similar to this. And I extracted two arrows for a man from the commanders of the Sultan; one of them had fallen into the middle of his nose, leaning slightly towards the right side.
The arrow completely disappeared, so I was called to treat him after the arrow fell for three days; I found that the wound of the arrow was very narrow, so I probed it with a thin wire but did not feel it. He had swelling and pain under his right ear due to the fracture.

Until it opened and healed, I felt the thin tip of the arrow that remained attached to the splinter. Then I increased the opening of the wound with that astringent medicine until the tip of the arrow appeared clearly to us, and it took about four months for me to remove it along with it.

The physicians used to say that his nasal polyp should not be cauterized, so I cauterized it and the wound healed, and the patient was cured completely without any pain or discomfort thereafter. And in every hour and at any time, except that children should not be purged until they reach fourteen years of age, nor should the elderly who have passed sixty years of age be purged; so if anyone is forced to undergo purging for any reason.
And it is necessary to cleanse the bowel before purging with a gentle enema if there is much retained feces, lest it attract to the veins at the time of purging from the bowel a harmful odor that harms the main organs; and the emaciated, diabetics, and those with diarrhea should not be purged until that passes from them.
Be careful of ejaculation after intercourse, as well as excessive sex, exertion, exercise, staying up late, fasting, and all other bodily or mental stresses. Then observe the effect on mixing before that if the blood is thick.
With food, drink, and medicine if possible, then he should enter the bathhouse if nothing prevents him or perform some exercise so that his blood becomes thin and his ejaculation occurs in the morning as we have said. It is also recommended that he avoids all mental stresses that day.
Avoid all mental stresses such as worries, anger, fear, and physical stresses like excessive exertion, frequent ejaculation, etc. Prepare your seating area with items that people usually use, such as pleasant scents, incense, cushions, and the like, to whatever extent possible for each person.
Then the ejaculator sits on a higher seat than that of the non-ejaculator, then he extends his arm and the ejaculator strokes it with his hand twice or thrice, then he tightens the ligature with a strap and loosens it twice or thrice, ensuring moderate tension.
When the tightness is not balanced, either by excess in binding which prevents blood flow or if it is too loose, it also prevents blood flow. Then after the binding, it is appropriate that the patient presses both hands together with both palms.
Until the veins swell and become palpable, then the practitioner should rub a little of the old oil on the area to be opened. He should place his left index finger on the same vein below the spot he intends to open slightly, so that the vein does not roll away from the incision. Because some veins, when cut, roll away from the incision and are filled with air, so when the practitioner places the knife on them, they sink beneath the knife and deceive the practitioner, and the knife does not open the vein, and even if it is opened, it is only slightly.
Therefore, it is necessary for the practitioner to be cautious and consider these things carefully. Then he should let the knife descend. If the vein does not open from its first pass, he should try again under that spot slightly or above it with a wheel if the place has not become tough.
If the patient is bitten or stung, leave him for a day or two and do not tighten the bandage, as it may draw out hot venom, and he should not enter the bath. Then, if desired, he can repeat the cupping. If the wound was caused by a scorpion and the opening is small with thin flowing blood.
And if you fear that not enough blood will come out, then prepare the wound in the same hole on a vertical position and slightly enlarge the opening. Do this with haste before the place swells, for many people may swell at the small opening.
If you see that it has swollen, do not apply the cupping glass again, as it will not help. Instead, place on it something of the oil of cumin, for it facilitates the flow of blood and is better in this situation than the oil itself and other ointments.
Use the oil of cumin in all your cuppings for the veins when the blood flow is difficult, and this can also be done with the juice of radish or wild rue if one of them is placed on the site, for then the blood will become thin and dissolve if it is thick.
In the case of a large wound in the rectal area, it often happens, especially if one has not had an enema before, or if the incision was small, that the wound becomes swollen and inflamed. Therefore, immediately apply a sponge soaked in warm water with a little salt to the wound, and leave it on for an hour; it will soften.
And you should do that after the bleeding has stopped completely, either from the same incision or another one. If there is any residue of blackness or greenness left in the area after several days, it is not harmful. Therefore, if you wish, you can apply some patience and dissolved myrrh to it.
Or something from the juice of the fig and similar things, for it often happens that there is swelling and inflammation when the bladder is opened. If you find it swollen upon your touch, then beware not to apply anything we have mentioned on it.
For it sometimes exudes thick blood, but you should compress it with what is in it to harden the area, then treat it with the rest of the treatments until it heals. It is necessary for each person's blood to be expelled according to their strength and what appears as the dominant color in the blood.
If the blood is dark, let it come out until it turns red; similarly, if you see it thick, send it out until it becomes thin; and similarly, if it is coagulated, until its coagulation disappears. And it is appropriate for someone who is strongly filled with blood and needs to expel the blood all at once.
To widen the orifice and make the wound broad; but for a weak person, it is better to do the opposite and let it come out in portions, with the hole being narrow. And the best tool to use for widening the orifice is one that is curved, smooth, and without any burrs.
This blow from the wound is safe from infection and cutting a nerve, as long as it is broad and long; and it should be habitual at the time of deep incision. For evacuation, if someone wants to empty the blood from their arm and relieve the second time of bleeding, it is necessary for one who has undergone surgery with significant loss of strength that the blood be released little by little according to his strength over consecutive days.
And if someone wants to empty their arm and relieve the blood again, and they are strong-bodied, let them do so after seven or nine hours from the first surgery; but if someone wants to draw the blood from one part of the body to another, it is necessary for him to be relieved on the second or third day.

Do not touch it until the inflammation settles; if necessity forces you to bleed again, then there is no choice but either to corrupt it above that place or to corrupt it in the other arm or vein.
As for corroding the cord of the arm, it is corroded as a substitute with vinegar or vitriol if they are not available or are scarce, because it is composed of them both.
